Step 10: Gain Support Points
You always gain 1 Support Point 
automatically� If your platoon leader 
accompanied you on the mission and did 
not become a casualty, gain an additional 
Support Point�
Support Points accumulate until 
you spend them� Track them on your 
campaign roster�
Step 11: Exposure
The longer you spend in this world, 
the more you begin to be a part of 
it� As that progresses, your soldiers 
will start to experience changes and 
develop fantastical abilities� Exposure 
is tracked for your squad as a whole, 
with all Exposure Points earned going 
into a single pool tracked on your 
campaign roster� 
You automatically earn 
1 point of Exposure in 
any mission that lasts 
for 3 battle rounds or 
longer� Certain events in 
the campaign can also 
award additional points 
of Exposure� Regardless 
of the source, they are 
pooled into a single resource 
pool until you spend them�
See the Transformations 
chapter (page 132) for ways to 
spend your Exposure points� 
Step 12: Loot
The world is full of marvelous magical 
things, from enchanted swords to 
alchemical potions, and stranger objects 
yet� After each battle, you may roll once 
on the Loot tables (see page 122) to see 
what you found�
Magical items tend to be attuned to 
willpower and determination (not to 
mention being lucky)� If you succeeded 
in your mission, you roll twice and 
then choose which of the items you 
want to receive� 
Missions may occasionally generate a 
bonus Objective when rolling for 
Sudden Death� If it did and you 
completed the additional Objective,  
you receive both items rolled on the 
Loot table�
There are other possibilities to obtain 
Loot which are detailed in the rules as 
they occur� 

---

## Page 124

RESOLUTION
122
Step 13: Gather Kit
You have only limited supplies available, 
but you just might be able to talk your 
way into some military goodies� Likewise, 
your soldiers will come across interesting 
things in monster lairs or bartered from 
villagers, and be able to kit-bash some 
much needed upgrades from scrap�
After every mission, you receive Kit Points 
and may spend them on any items you like 
from the Kit List table below� Kit Points 
can be saved up� 
Earning Kit Points
You receive 1D6 Kit Points every mission 
as long as the mission lasted for at least 
3 battle rounds� If you win, you may roll 
twice and pick the better score�
All items must be carried by a specific 
character to be usable� Characters can 
carry only one of a specific type of kit, but 
can carry multiple types� 
Kit List table
Kit Cost Effects
Medical pack 2 Extra bandages and painkillers.
Single use as a Free Action� Remove 1 Stun marker 
from up to 2 different soldiers within 6"�
Melee weapon 2 A sturdy sword or axe. 
Counts as a sword in hand-to-hand combat�
Heavy melee weapon 3 A sturdy sword or axe that is also quite large.
Counts as a large sword in hand-to-hand combat� 
The soldier cannot carry a squad automatic or 
anti-tank weapon�
Lucky trinket 6 Lucky trading game card or similar. 
Grant 1 point of Luck to a soldier that has none� 
Only usable once and a soldier cannot carry multiple 
at the same time�
Armor 3 Padded coat or mail shirt.
6+ saving throw�
Heavy armor 4 Coat of plates, brigandine, or similar armor.
5+ saving throw but -1" movement�
Ephemera 3 Stuff they’d probably sell in a new age shop.
Single use� As a Free Action, increase Power by +2 for 
spell-casting� Only one Ephemera can be used by a 
character per battle round�
Assorted tools 2 Maps, tools, and other stuff that might come in 
handy.
Single use� You may reroll one Wits test�

## Page 125

RESOLUTION
123
Step 14: Sort Out Your Equipment
Once you know what your squad will look 
like for the next battle, you can rearrange 
your weapons and equipment� If you had 
casualties, their weapons remain available 
to you and can be reassigned� The primary 
weapons of your squad are the assault 
rifle, submachine gun, and shotgun� Each 
figure with one of these primary weapons 
allows you to take one soldier armed with 
a squad automatic, sharpshooter’s rifle, 
or grenade launcher�
One sharpshooter’s rifle can be 
swapped for a grenade launcher or the 
other way around�
One soldier with an assault rifle, sub-
machine gun, or shotgun can swap for 
another of those three options�
Magic items and mission gear can be 
stashed or issued to any soldiers you like� 
Items that are stashed can be retrieved 
after any future mission� 
Note that magical items can be alluring: 
If you want to transfer a magic item from 
a soldier who currently has it (whether 
to the Stash – see boxout, above – or 
to another soldier) and they are not 
currently recovering from injuries, roll 
1D6� On a 1, they refuse to do so, though 
you may try again after a future battle� 
Step 15: Update the Map
After fighting through a region, it can be 
marked as clear using any method you 
like, such as crossing it out or planting 
a flag on the map� Your actions have 
helped the people living here gather 
their strength and retake the region 
from the monsters� 
Step 16: Get Ready
You are now done with your campaign 
turn and ready to begin the next one!
Review the Campaign Flow (see page 67) 
to see what is happening next� If the turn 
you completed was before Turn 12, the 
next turn is waiting for you� Some players 
prefer to prepare the next mission in 
advance before they stop for the day, 
while others enjoy doing that as part of 
the next day of gaming�
If you just completed Turn 12, turn to 
Final Battles (page 94) to find out how it 
is all going to go down� 
The Stash
As you play, you may end up with items 
you don’t have a specific use for at that 
moment� These go in your Stash� The Stash 
is the pool of gear you have available, but 
which is kept at the base� At this point, any 
excess items can be left in the Stash, and 
stashed items can be retrieved for use� 
Items in the Stash cannot be used during a 
mission but are safe and cannot be lost�

## Page 126

RESOLUTION
124
LOOT
One end of the staff had been carved into the head of a dragon, its snout wide and toothy 
and malevolent, its carved eyes glittering with dark destruction. Even the wood itself 
was unsettling, its patterns and whorls seeming more like other places than mere 
textures in the grain. Worlds and hidden rooms if you looked close enough.
– Forgotten Ruin
When the rules say you have earned one 
or more Loot rolls, they are resolved using 
the tables in this chapter� Roll D100 for 
each Loot roll and check the tables to see 
what item you receive� All rolls lead to 
sub-tables that require an additional roll�
When you win a mission, you may roll 
twice and pick� Determine all details of 
each item before choosing�
Items are either Consumable or 
Permanent� Assume all items are 
Permanent unless described as 
Consumable� Consumable items do 
not have to be carried by a specific 
character and can be used at any time 
by any member of your squad� Using a 
Consumable item is a Free Action� 
Permanent items cannot be used until 
they have been assigned to a character� 
This is normally done during the 
campaign post-battle sequence� If you find 
an item during a battle, it can be issued 
immediately to any character within 2" 
of the point where it was found, and used 
right away� Otherwise, it is added to your 
campaign Stash� 
Permanent items may grant bonuses to 
specific functions, act as weapons, or give 
special abilities that can be activated� 
Each item will explain if it is used 
automatically, or requires a Free Action or 
a Combat Action to use�
A character can carry any number of 
Permanent items but cannot use more 
than one for any given action� For 
example, even if you have three magic 
swords you are lugging around, you will 
have to pick which one you use when 
you fight in a hand-to-hand combat, 
though you could switch swords between 
combats if desired�
Typically, you will do better if you share 
your items throughout the squad to 
maximize their benefits�
Specific Carry (realism option)
Players who struggle with the abstraction 
of unassigned items moving between 
figures may prefer that Consumable items 
are carried by specific soldiers and can 
only be used by that soldier�  
Form Factors Do Not Matter
Other than the general category of item, 
the exact form factor is not important 
to the game and a given magic item can 
take any form you like� This is particularly 
useful for players that want their 
miniatures to closely resemble their in-
game reality�

## Page 127

RESOLUTION
125
Loot table
D100 Item group
01-20 Magical Weapons and subtable 
(right and page 126)
21-35 Magical Armors (see Magical 
Armors subtable, page 127)
36-45 Scrolls (see Scrolls subtable, 
page 128)
46-65 Potions (see Potions subtable, 
page 128)
66-80 Staffs (see Staffs subtable,  
page 130)
81-00 Various (see Various Items 
subtable, page 130)
Magical Weapons
Weapons must be carried by a character 
to be usable� Each weapon is indicated as 
being either a melee weapon or a missile 
weapon and can only be used in the 
appropriate type of combat�
A D6 can be rolled on the following 
subtables to determine the nature of a 
particular melee or missile weapon, if you 
like� This is only for flavor purposes and 
another option may be to determine the 
characteristics first and then decide what 
form the weapon takes� A character with a 
magical melee weapon is not considered 
to be unarmed in hand-to-hand combat 
and does not suffer the -1 penalty to hand-
to-hand combat�
Magical missiles use the normal Hit roll 
and benefit from Combat Skill as well as 
magical bonuses�

on each of the Weapon Type, Hit Bonus,

D6 Weapon type

4-5 +2

shooting a missile weapon and the hand-

D6 Damage bonus
1-2 +1
3 +2
4-5 +1 normally, +3 versus monsters 
and champions�
6 +1 and Hits twice
The damage bonus is added to the roll 
against Toughness�

below:
Magical Weapon Special Ability subtables
D6 Melee abilities
1 Quickness� Once per phase, you 
may follow up into contact and 
fight again�
2 Parrying� You may force the 
enemy to reroll one hand-to-
hand roll per phase�
3 Deep strikes� A roll of a 6 in 
hand-to-hand combat inflicts 2 
Hits� 
4 Strength� Cannot be Stunned�
5 Guarding� 6+ saving throw�
6 Slaying� If the weapon 
successfully damages a monster, 
it loses 1 additional MP�
D6 Missile abilities
1 Destruction� Roll twice for 
damage and pick the best score� 
Against monsters, Hit twice 
instead�
2 Piercing� Ignore saving throws� 
3 Keenness� A 6 on the damage 
roll inflicts 2 additional Hits on 
the target�
4 Fear� If the shot kills a figure in 
a mob, roll 2 additional Morale 
dice� 
5 Seeking� If you have Line of 
Sight, the target always counts as 
being in the open and visibility 
limits do not apply�  
6 Impact� Non-monster targets 
are Knocked Down when 
struck�

Magical Armors
Armor must be carried by a character to 
be usable� Each character can wear only 
one piece of armor and cannot remove it 
or replace it during a battle� You cannot 
combine magical and regular armor� The 
exact form of the armor is up to you; it 
may be a mail shirt, a chest plate, helmet, 
or anything else you like�
All armor from this table provides a 
5+ saving throw�
Magical Armors subtable
D100 Armor
01-15 Armor of Movement
16-30 Armor of Deflection
31-40 Armor of Brightness
41-55 Armor of Sturdiness
56-65 Armor of Retaliation
66-80 Armor of Alliance
81-90 Armor of Hurry
91-00 Armor of Resilience
Armor of Alliance
A stalwart protective item that 
emboldens your friends.
All friends within 6" gain a 6+ saving 
throw�
Armor of Brightness
When enemies are near, this armor 
shines with a fierce brightness though the 
shine is only visible to your enemies.
Hand-to-hand opponents that roll a 
1 on the combat dice lose the fight 
automatically and take 1 additional Hit to 
the normal outcome of the melee�
Armor of Deflection
Arrows deflect right off the surface of 
this armor.
All archery Hits on the character must 
reroll the Hit die once�
Armor of Hurry
A coat of armor that seems to implore 
you to get into the fight.
The saving throw always matches the 
battle round number: 1+ in Round 1; 
2+ in Round 2; and so forth�
Armor of Movement
A particularly light suit of armor. It 
actually enhances your ability to move.
Adds +1" to normal movement and +1" to 
Dash movement�
Armor of Resilience
This armor repels almost anything that 
strikes it.
Your Toughness counts as 1 point greater 
than normal (to a maximum of 6)� 
Armor of Retaliation
Brimming with malevolent magic, 
this armor seeks to destroy those that 
attack it.
If the character is struck in hand-to-hand 
combat, the attacker also takes a Hit with 
the same damage modifiers and effects�
Armor of Sturdiness
This armor is extremely heavy, but the 
material is particularly dense and solid.
The character cannot Dash, but the 
armor provides a 4+ saving throw and 
the wearer cannot be Knocked Down 
for any reason�

## Page 130

128
Scrolls
Scrolls have spells on them� For each spell 
on a scroll, roll once on the Spell table 
(see page 52)� A scroll may have multiple 
copies of the same spell if you roll the 
same result� 
Scrolls are Consumable items but require 
a normal Interact Action to use� Select 
one spell on any of your scrolls and cast it 
as if the character taking the Action was 
casting it� The spell is automatically cast 
with the exact Power required� 
Each spell can be cast once only�
Scrolls subtable
D100 Scroll
01-25 1 spell
26-45 2 spells
46-55 3 spells
56-65 1 spell� If the spell has a range 
in inches, double it�
66-75 1 spell� If the spell affects a set 
number of targets, double it�
76-85 1 spell� If it normally could be 
resisted, it cannot�
86-95 2 spells, but you can cast only 
one of them
96-00 4 spells
Potions
Potions are Consumable items� Any 
character may drink a potion as a 
Free Action, and the effects are applied 
immediately� Some potions can be used 
outside of combat if the rules say so�
If the entry says “2x” it means you find 
two potions� 
You can try to drink less of a potion� If 
so, roll 1D6� On a 1-2, it has no effect, 
and the entire potion is now used� On a 
3-6, you can get one more use out of the 
potion before it is all gone� A potion will 
never give more than one additional use 
through this rule�
Potions subtable
D100 Potion
01-15 Healing
16-20 2x Healing
21-35 Strength
36-45 Leaping
46-55 Ghost Form
56-65 Fire Breath
66-75 Shrinking
76-80 Unidentified potion
81-85 2x Unidentified potions
86-95 Holy water
96-00 Unstable potion�
Fire Breath
A delicious concoction, heavy on ginger.
The character immediately spews a burst 
of flame� Draw out a straight line 6" long: 
Any figure touched by the line is struck 
with +2 damage� Undead (including 
vampires) are Hit twice�

## Page 131

RESOLUTION
129
Ghost Form
A translucent drink, slightly minty.
The character cannot attack or be attacked 
except by spells� They cannot pick up 
items, but anything they currently carry 
can be kept� Ghost form characters 
can move through terrain features 
unhindered but cannot climb up on 
things, and will fall harmlessly to the 
ground if they are on a terrain feature 
when they drink the potion�
Each time the character activates, roll a 
D6: On a 1, the potion expires� If it expires 
within a solid obstacle, you become a 
casualty�
Healing
A rejuvenating elixir, tasting faintly like 
berries.
Can be given to a character after a battle 
to ignore one roll on the Injury table� 
This must be used before rolling on the 
Injury table�
Holy water
You are definitely not meant to drink this.
This can be thrown at an Undead 
mob within 6"� Roll 4D6, with each 
4-6 destroying one figure in the mob 
automatically� The figures closest to the 
thrower are Hit first� If thrown at an 
Undead monster, each 4+ inflicts  
1 Monster Point of damage� No saving 
throws apply.
If you find holy water from an 
“Unidentified” potion, you may keep it 
until you are ready to use it�
Leaping
A slimy draught with an acrid smell.
Instead of moving normally, the character 
can leap up to 6" in a straight line� They 
may leap up onto terrain features, down 
from features, or across gaps or figures�
Shrinking
It only has a slight taste.
The character becomes tiny� They can 
move at only half speed but cannot attack 
or be attacked while tiny� The potion lasts 
for this and 2 more activations� 
Strength
A thick brew, bubbling disconcertingly.
For the rest of the mission, the character 
adds +1 to both Combat Skill and damage 
rolls in hand-to-hand combat only, and 
will Knock Down any non-monster foes 
they strike� They may move and fire with 
weapons with the Heavy trait�
Unidentified potion
This could be anything, really.
The effect is unknown though you 
can make some guesses� When drunk, 
roll again on this table to determine 
the effects of the potion� If you roll 
“Unidentified” or “Unstable”, you may pick 
any potion type you would like it to be� 
Unstable potion
The smell is a bit off.
Roll again on this table to determine 
the type� If you roll “Unidentified” or 
“Unstable”, you may pick any potion type 
you like� When you choose to drink the 
potion, roll 1D6� On a 1, it turns out it 
didn’t work at all�

Staffs
Staffs are Permanent items and must 
be carried by a character to be used� A 
character can only carry a single staff� 
You can use the staff as an Action� Some 
staffs have limited uses� If so, you must 
keep track and once it is used up, it is 
destroyed� 
Staffs with per battle uses last 
indefinitely, but unused activations 
cannot be saved up�
Staffs cannot be used in hand-to-hand 
combat�
Staffs subtable
D100 Staff
01-15 Illumination (1D6+3 uses)
16-40 Fire Bolt (1D6+1 uses)
41-50 Paralysis (1 use per battle)
51-60 Recovery (1 use per campaign 
turn)
61-70 Petty Air Elemental (1 use per 
battle)
71-100 Lightning Bolt (1D6+1 uses)
Fire Bolt
A target point within Line of Sight is 
struck by the bolt� A figure struck directly 
takes 3 Hits with +2 damage�
All figures within 2" are Hit once for +0 
damage�
Undead figures take 1 additional Hit in 
both cases�
Illumination
For the rest of the battle, all visibility 
penalties are removed�
Lightning Bolt
Draw a line 18" long� Any figure it 
passes through is Hit for +1 damage� 
Monsters are Hit twice� The bolt stops 
when it contacts a terrain feature� Non-
monster figures are also Knocked Down�
Paralysis
A single figure within Line of Sight cannot 
move or attack when next activated� If 
targeting a monster, it cannot move but 
can make missile attacks if normally able� 
Petty Air Elemental
When used, two friendly characters 
within 12" and Line of Sight can swap 
positions� 
Recovery
A single soldier recovering from injuries 
may reduce their recovery time by 
1 campaign turn�
Various Items
Items in this category can be almost 
anything� Read the descriptions of the 
items carefully� Permanent items (P) must 
be carried by a character to be usable�

D100 Item Uses

Chime of Disappearance
Usable twice� The user and any soldiers 
of choice within 9" are immediately 
removed from the battle� If they were 
the last soldiers on the battlefield, the 
mission ends� Note that this does not 
affect enemy figures�
Cloak of Distortion
Continuous while worn� The wearer 
cannot be shot at by enemies more than 
9" away�
Dust of Evasion
Single use. Used before a battle to give 
every soldier in the squad a 5+ saving 
throw for one entire battle�
Enchanted Oil
Permanent� Any one weapon of choice 
can be enchanted if it is not already 
enchanted or magical� The weapon adds 
+1 to all Hit and damage rolls� Weapons 
with multiple shots receive this bonus to 
only a single shot per attack�
Horn of Horrors
Single use� Select a mob within Line of 
Sight and roll 10 Morale dice against it� 
Any survivors become Fearless for the 
rest of the battle�
Leaping Boots
Continuous while worn� The character 
does not move any faster, but can move 
through the air, landing on terrain 
features within movement range and 
ignoring terrain as they go� They can also 
move “through” any human-sized figures�
Magic Hourglass
Single use� Select up to 3 soldiers within 
6" and Line of Sight� One may be the user 
of the item� Each soldier immediately 
activates� These activations are a bonus 
in addition to their normal activations in 
the round�
Stone of Shattering
Single use� Select a terrain feature within 
9" and Line of Sight� It crumbles into 
rubble� All figures within or touching the 
feature take a +0 damage Hit� Figures 
above ground level fall as well� All affected 
figures are Knocked Down�
Summoning Chime
Usable twice� Roll on the Monster 
table (page 107): The indicated creature 
shows up anywhere within 6" of the 
user and fights on your side for the rest 
of the battle� It activates in the Slow 
Actions Phase�
Pearls of Time
Usable twice� Target a figure within 6" and 
Line of Sight� They are frozen in time for 
the rest of the current and all of the next 
battle round� While frozen, they cannot 
take any actions and cannot be attacked or 
targeted by spells or items in any way�
None of their abilities apply,  
e�g� Aggression increases�
Sorcerous Tool
Permanent� If carried by a wizard, they 
add +1 to their Power score each round� 
For example, if their Reaction die was a 3, 
they have a Power of 4�

TRANSFORMATIONS
When I began to dream in Elvish, it was then I knew I could speak it. 
And it was when the orc horde overran one of the fighting positions along 
First Platoon's sector on the east side of the island the Rangers were defending 
that I knew we weren't in Kansas anymore.
– Forgotten Ruin
Transformations allow your soldiers to 
truly become part of the fantasy world� 
Whether it is learning to cast spells or 
assuming a fantastical form, the result is 
sure to be spectacular� 
Transformations are earned with 
Exposure Points� These are earned as  
you take on missions as explained in the 
Post-Battle Sequence (see page 114), as 
well as from a range of other sources�  
At your discretion, it costs 3 or 4 Exposure 
Points to earn a Transformation (see 
below)� The Transformation always 
happens to a random soldier who does 
not already have one� 
Transformations will occasionally match 
up with the outlook and talent of a 
particular soldier: 
  If you paid 3 points, you roll once 
on the table below and receive the 
result of the roll� 
  If you paid 4 points, you roll twice 
and can pick either result� If you roll 
the same result twice, you must pick 
that one� 
No Spell-caster in the Squad?
If none of your soldiers can cast spells 
currently, you may opt to take The Arcane 
instead of rolling randomly� Please note 
that you cannot roll and then opt to pick 
The Arcane� 


---

## Page 135

RESOLUTION
133
Transformation Upgrades
Once the magical change has begun, it 
seldom stops� The nerd in the platoon may 
enjoy pointing out that this is “just like 
that card game I play” but whatever the 
reason, you have to understand what this 
offers to be successful in battle�
All Transformations can be upgraded by 
spending additional Exposure Points� As 
long as you have the available points, you 
may do so at any point, even mid-battle� 
Apply any new abilities immediately� 
Main Transformation table
D100 Transformation
01-11 The Arcane
12-19 The Centaur
20-28 The Cursed
29-38 The Divine
39-48 The Green
49-58 The Minotaur
59-68 The Savage
69-76 The Scaled
77-86 The Scoundrel
87-93 The Skyborne
94-00 The Swarm
The Arcane (wizard, etc.)
The character is blessed with arcane 
insight�
  Randomly select 3 spells that the 
character can use from now on�
  Future advancements for this 
character must be used to buy  
new spells�
Upgrades:
The Sight: [+1 Exposure] Add +2 to the 
Wits score of the character�
Spell Acquisition: [+3 Exposure]  
The character immediately learns any 
spell of your choice�
Apprentice: [+2 Exposure] One character 
with no Transformations becomes Arcane 
themselves and begins with 1 spell 
selected at random from those known by 
this character� 
The Miniatures Challenge
Of course, you will need a suitable 
miniature to use for the new soldier� 
This can be solved by using an 
appropriate figure from a fantasy 
role-playing game, but enterprising 
modelers can get a lot of fun out of 
kit-bashing minotaurs with rocket 
launchers and so forth� The entries 
are open-ended, so you can exercise 
as much creativity as possible in 
adapting cool miniatures�

The Centaur
The bad news about having a horse body 
is that you need two pairs of boots.
  The character increases their Speed 
by +2" when moving in a straight 
line and always adds +3" to their 
Dash moves.
  Another soldier can ride on their 
back and will move when the 
centaur moves. Shooting from 
horseback counts the shooter’s 
Combat Skill as +0. Mounting up 
or dismounting takes an action. If 
the centaur becomes a casualty, the 
rider is placed where they fell.
  In hand-to-hand combat, only the 
centaur fights, not any mounted 
soldier (your soldiers are not  
trained knights) but you may add 
any magical weapon bonus of  
either character (only one weapon 
can be picked).
Upgrades:
  Stomp: [+1 Exposure] If a hand-to-
hand combat by rider or centaur 
ends in a draw, the centaur can 
decide to Stomp. The soldiers are  
not Hit, and the target is Hit with 
+0 damage (regardless of any  
weapons used).
  Leap: [+2 Exposure] The soldier 
may replace a Dash move 
with a Leap of 1D6+1". 
The Leap must be in 
a straight line and 
can clear any figures 
or obstacles up to 
normal human 
height. A rider can 
be dropped off at any 
point of the Leap. 
The Cursed (Werewolf, 
Weretiger, Wereboar, etc.)
The character can shape-shift into a 
dangerous animal such as a tiger or wolf.
Shapeshifting takes an action and must 
be done after the battle has started. No 
die roll is required. The character cannot 
change back during the battle.
  While in animal form, the character 
cannot use any weapons but has 
natural melee weapons (teeth and 
claws) adding +1 to both the Combat 
Skill and damage rolls. They Hit 
twice versus any monster.
  The character can add their full 
movement when Dashing in animal 
form, instead of only moving +3".
  The character receives a 6+ saving 
throw against all attacks in both 
human and animal form.
Upgrades:
  Brutal attack: [+1 Exposure]  
In animal form, if the character  
rolls a natural 6 on the damage 
roll, the target does not receive any 
saving throws. 
  Regeneration: [+2 Exposure]  
The character cannot be 
Stunned, and rolls twice, 
picking the best result, when 
rolling for post-battle 
injuries. This benefit 
applies in human 
form too.

The Divine (Cleric, Paladin, etc.)
The character is suffused with divine 
energy�
  The character may negate any 
magical attack aimed at themselves 
or a soldier within 6" and Line of 
Sight on a D6 roll of a 4+� 
  Once per battle when another 
soldier within 6" would become 
a casualty, the Divine soldier may 
recite a chant or prayer, negating the 
Hit completely� Only one character 
can be protected in this fashion even 
if the attack struck multiple targets�
Upgrades:
  Inspire Awe: [+1 Exposure] When 
the character activates, select a mob 
within 6" and roll 3 Morale dice� 
The effect applies even if the mob 
would be Fearless or is otherwise 
unaffected by Morale tests, 
though champions remain 
immune as normal� 
  Divine Aura: 
[+2 Exposure] 
 The character and 
all allies within  
6" receive a  
6+ saving throw�
The Green (Elf, Halfling, 
Plant Person, etc.)
The character feels a new connection to 
the wild things�
  They do not suffer any terrain 
penalties due to forest or other 
natural features and ignore all 
darkness penalties�
  The character receives a bow and 
may shoot it in place of a military 
weapon� Unlike enemy bows, the 
character adds their Combat Skill to 
shots� They strike with +1 damage, 
ignores Cover, and a natural 6 to Hit 
will ignore saving throws�
Upgrades:
  Keen Archery: [+1 Exposure]  
When stationary, the character may 
shoot twice when using their bow or 
any magical ranged weapon� 
  Infiltration: [+2 Exposure]  
The character may choose to begin 
the game off the battlefield� They are 
assigned Initiative dice normally� 
When they are active, they may 
choose to remain off the table or to 
arrive� When they arrive randomly, 
select a soldier on the battlefield, 
then place the Infiltrator anywhere 
you like within 6" of them� The 
Infiltrator cannot move 
when they arrive, but 
may shoot (counting as 
stationary) or be placed 
directly into hand-to-hand 
combat� All shooting and hand-
to-hand combat rolls receive a 
+1 on the round they arrive�

The Minotaur
The character wakes up as a hulking  
half-bull beast�
  They can move and fire normally 
with weapons with the Heavy trait, 
and, if engaging in hand-to-hand 
combat during their activation, they 
may roll the combat dice twice and 
pick the best score�
  They increase their Toughness score 
by +1 (maximum 6)�
Upgrades:
  Hulk: [+2 Exposure] The character 
ignores the first Hit each battle 
that would make them become a 
casualty�
  Horns: [+1 Exposure] The character 
has a natural melee weapon that 
Hits for +1 damage� 
The Savage (Hyena-folk, etc.)
The character's bestial nature expresses 
itself in bestial features: claws, fangs, and 
bloodthirst�
  Increase Toughness by +1  
(maximum 6)�
  The character can enter hand-to-
hand combat with a Follow Up move 
and may fight immediately when 
doing so� This can occur only once 
per phase� 
  When fighting monsters in hand-
to-hand combat, a natural 6 on the 
damage roll allows another damage 
die to be rolled (and thus additional 
Monster Points to be lost)� This can 
trigger multiple times� 
Upgrades:
  War Cry: [+1 Exposure] Any mob 
that tests Morale for any reason 
within 8" of the soldier must add 
one additional die to the number 
rolled�
  Blood Instincts: [+2 Exposure] 
The soldier rolls two dice in 
hand-to-hand combat and 
picks the best of the dice� 
If both dice score a 6, an 
additional Hit is inflicted 
(for a total of 3 due to the 
Great Hit rule)�

The Scaled (Lizard-folk,  
Fish-folk, etc.)
Covered in heavy scales, with a thick, 
spiny, or finned tail�
  The Scaled get a 6+ saving throw 
against Hits and do not suffer any 
movement penalties in water or 
swamp features, including Swamp 
regional terrain�
  They can move at normal pace 
through Impassable water features 
though they cannot attack or be 
attacked while within a water 
feature�

  Tail Slap: [+2 Exposure]  
After successfully striking a mob 
enemy in hand-to-hand combat, you

and another figure of the same mob 
within 1"�
  Cold-blooded: [+1 Exposure]

penalties from being in Desert

  Thick Scales:

The saving 
throw is 
improved

The Scoundrel (Thief, Bard, etc.)
The character has gained a strange 
combination of luck and foolishness�
The character cannot receive a saving 
throw due to armor or any other type of 
protection� Instead, whenever anything 
hostile strikes the character, such as 
an attack or spell, they may attempt to 
Dodge� Roll 1D6, with 5-6 avoiding the 
threat and allowing the character to 
move a single base move in any direction 
immediately� The Dodge roll is not a 
saving throw and cannot be negated by 
attacks that prevent saves, nor can it be 
modified up or down by any effect or rule� 
Dodging applies to all types of traps and 
natural hazards�  
Upgrades:
  Thieves’ Luck: [+1 Exposure] 
Whenever the character makes 
a Wits test of any kind, they may 
opt to reroll if they do not like the 
result� The Wits reroll has a fixed 
+1 modifier, regardless of what the 
actual score was� Other modifiers 
apply normally�
  Silent Movement: [+1 Exposure]  
If the character does not shoot when 
they activate, they are hidden and 
cannot be shot at or targeted by 
spells until the Scoundrel activates 
again� They can be attacked 
normally in hand-to-hand combat 
and can be targeted normally by 
enemy archers or spell-casters 
within 8"� Note that an enemy that 
is not within 8" will ignore the 
Scoundrel for all purposes� 
  Use Cover: [+1 Exposure]  
If the Scoundrel is in Cover, they 
can Dodge archery attacks on a  
4+ instead of the customary 5+�

The Skyborne (any Variety of 
Bird-person)
The character has a huge pair of wings 
allowing limited flight�
  They no longer take any falling 
damage, and can ignore obstacles, 
chasms, and terrain penalties when 
moving�
  They may add 3" to the range of any 
thrown hand grenades�
  If on a raised terrain feature, the 
character can glide instead of 
moving normally� The character 
lands on any lower position (or the 
ground) within a horizontal distance 
equal to double the height of their 
position� For example, if they are 3" 
above ground level, they could land 
anywhere within 6" (measured on 
the ground)�
Upgrades:
  Wing Buffet: [+1 Exposure]  
Any opponent that rolls a 1 on 
their hand-to-hand combat dice is 
Knocked Down� They take 1 Hit, in 
addition to any normal outcomes of 
the battle�
  Take to the Sky: [+2 Exposure] 
The character may fly into the sky 
by spending both their Move and 
their Action� On any subsequent 
activation, they can land anywhere 
on the table as a Move and take 
an action normally� The character 
cannot use any flying abilities at all 
for the next two battle rounds� 
The Swarm (Mantis-folk,  
Spider-folk, etc.)
A horror with a chitinous exo-skeleton 
and multiple limbs�
  Receive a 5+ saving throw versus all 
Hits, and immunity to all types of 
poison attacks�
Upgrades:
  Venomous: [+2 Exposure]  
Enemies that are Hit in hand-to-
hand combat roll twice against 
Toughness and use the worst result� 
This does not work against Undead�
  Multi-limbed: [+1 Exposure]  
The character can use two weapons 
in hand-to-hand combat� Apply the 
damage and any magical abilities of 
one weapon only (but the character 
can choose each melee), and add a +1 
modifier when rolling for hand-to-
hand combat to account for the other 
weapon� When fighting with two 
weapons, the character adds +1 to 
saving throws against hand-to-hand 
combat Hits� 
  Chitinous: [+1 Exposure] 
The saving throw improves to 4+�


---

## Page 141

RESOLUTION
139
CAMPAIGN END
Outside it was dark now. The air was getting cold. And the island and the forest 
were dead silent. No drums. Not even the smell of smoke from out there in the woods. 
But you could feel something coming. Feel the length of the long night already 
stretching out into a never-seeing-the-sun-rise-again moment.
You could feel that they were coming now. Coming for us.
– Forgotten Ruin
Did you win the final battle? You 
emerge triumphantly as the evil keep 
collapses around you� Blood-soaked 
and battered, you have freed this world 
from a grave evil and can enjoy a few 
moments of quiet�
Did your squad all fall? Your heroic 
efforts have allowed the locals to mount 
an assault and drive the enemy out of 
their lands� Your wounded soldiers are 
rescued from the rubble and thanked 
profusely for their effects�
Either way, the survivors are able to 
recuperate, gather their thoughts, and 
make contact with the rest of the ranger 
force� Your adventure has come to an 
end… for now�
When you have played out the conclusion, 
the campaign has come to an end� Reflect 
on how you came out of it, how your 
favorite characters did, what your favorite 
moments were, and what it all felt like�
All unspent resources such as Story 
Points, Support Points, Kit Points, and so 
forth are lost�
All kit, weapons, and magic items are 
discarded, even if currently carried by a 
character� 
You now tally up your Victory Points to 
see how well you performed:
Outcome Victory Points
Every mission where 
you completed your 
Objectives
1 VP
Every villain defeated 1 VP
Every Special Mission 
completed
Additional 
+1 VP
Final Battle won Additional 
+2 VP
All awards are cumulative� 
Please note that the Artifact battles do not 
award any Victory Points, but the final 
battle does� 
If you achieve fewer than 5 Victory Points, 
the campaign has ended in defeat� You 
may save a single soldier of your choice to 
the veteran roster (see page 140)�
Victory Point Modifier
When determining your Victory Points at 
the end of the campaign, a multiplier is 
used� The multiplier starts at x1.0� Each 
point of Difficulty Factor changes it ±0.1 
up or down�
For example, if you earn 8 Victory Points 
and used a Difficulty Factor of +2, you 
would multiply by 1.2 for a final Victory 
Point score of 9.6�

---

## Page 142

RESOLUTION
140
In future campaigns you should strive to 
beat your prior best score, but as long as 
you end up with at least 5 Victory Points, 
you succeed� 
Story Point Bonus
Every 4 Victory Points you earned gives 
you one additional Story Point which 
may be listed on your veteran roster� 
These can be taken at any point in any 
future campaign� When each is used 
up, it is gone and will not be replaced, 
though there is no limit to how many 
you can earn over the course of playing 
multiple campaigns�
Final Advances
For every 6 Victory Points you earned, 
you receive one Final Advance� This can 
be taken as either an experience advance, 
or an upgrade for a Transformation 
(regardless of cost)� It can be applied to 
any soldier just like a regular 
advance, turning them into 
a known personality in the 
process, and allows you to get 
one of your grunts up to 
speed so they can be 
a more attractive 
option on your roster 
in a future campaign�
Create or Update Your 
Veteran Roster
If you won (5+ Victory Points achieved), 
you may save any of your soldiers to 
your veteran roster, a sheet of past 
soldiers you may choose to use in future 
campaigns (you may dedicate a spare 
platoon sheet to this purpose)� You are 
not required to save all of them if you 
only want to keep certain soldiers� For 
example, a grunt that never gained any 
advances may not be important to keep�
If you lost (fewer than 5 Victory Points), 
you may save just ONE soldier of your 
choice�
When you begin a new campaign, you 
may pick up to two soldiers from your 
veteran roster to carry over� 
When saving a character roster, include 
any Final Advances from this section, 
but do not save any kit, equipment, or 
magical items obtained� Such things must 
be earned again in the new campaign� 
In essence, what you are saving is the 
character profile and any skills and 
Transformations gained� Upgraded 
Transformations are saved 
in their upgraded form�

## Page 144

APPENDICES
142
MY GAME DID SOMETHING 
STRANGE!
The game may throw some unexpected 
elements your way� If you are not sure 
how to proceed, this section provides a 
few pointers:
A game event may refer to something 
that is not possible, such as an increase 
in Aggression in a mission that does 
not use the Aggression rule� If so, any 
impossible parts of the effect are simply 
ignored� For example, the Loot result on 
the Investigation table causes 2 points of 
Aggression to be earned, which would be 
ignored in the first two campaign turns; 
however, you would still receive the Loot�
If a lot of things appear to be happening 
simultaneously and it is getting confusing, 
stand back and resolve things in the order 
in which they were initiated� If you work 
through things one at a time you will 
usually be able to make sense of it�
If two things appear to make each other 
impossible, whichever was initiated 
first should take precedent� If they are 
completely even, try to do your best� In 
most cases you can either let the events 
cancel out or you could roll randomly to 
pick which takes precedent�
Remember that events do not stack 
up� For example, one figure moving 
or attacking may make it possible (or 
impossible) for another figure to do 
something they were previously intending 
to do that round� For example, if a figure 
makes an attack that kills an opponent, 
another figure could now move through 
that space or select a different target�
Key 'rule of thumb’: In general, 
special cases supersede regular cases� 
If an item or ability modifies 
how a core rule works, the item 
or ability takes precedent�


---

## Page 145

APPENDICES
143
MINIATURES
Selecting Miniatures
You will need two batches of miniatures 
to play the campaign: Military figures 
for the soldiers and fantasy figures for 
the bad guys� Luckily, both are readily 
available on the market� For military 
figures you can use figures from cold war 
and modern-day wargames ranges while 
any range of fantasy figures will do just 
fine� As figure ranges often fall out of 
availability and companies occasionally 
close up business, we have opted not to 
make specific recommendations here� 
Figures are usually described as being in 
a particular scale, such as 15mm or 28mm� 
This is the height of the figure, typically 
measured from the feet to the eye level� 
Note, however, that manufacturers often 
have some variation from each other and 
two figures that are both nominally 15mm 
may in fact not fit perfectly together, 
though on a gaming table the differences 
are usually not a big deal�
15mm figures are very popular for 
historical gaming and are quite cheap� 
They also do not take up a substantial 
amount of storage space and will allow 
your gaming table to feel quite large� 
28mm is the scale associated with many 
fantasy and science fiction miniatures 
games� These figures are often elaborate, 
and reward effort when painting them 
in detail�
Both will work well for your collection 
and will offer you a range of options� 
Even if you opt to use 3D printed figures 
instead of purchasing metal, resin, or 
plastic figures, they are usually indicated 
as being best for a particular scale� 
There are other scales, such as 6mm and 
10mm, though they are less common for 
skirmish gaming� 
Plastic figures for model builders are 
usually indicated as 1:72 scale, 1:35, or 
similar� These figures are quite cheap and 
can make good gaming figures, though 
finding fantasy creatures can be very 
difficult� Nominally, 1:72 figures should fit 
fairly well with 20mm metal figures� 
When buying monsters in particular, 
don’t neglect that a figure can often work 
out of scale� A small but mean lizard in 
28mm scale can be a fearsome monster 
on a 15mm battlefield, for example� 
Suitable gaming figures can often be 
found in unusual places: Toy stores often 
have containers full of plastic lizards, 
frogs, insects, and so on which make 
excellent monsters to fight� 
If physical miniatures are not your style, 
you can also find sets of print-and-play 
paper miniatures available for sale� Many 
of these are aimed at roleplaying gamers, 
so fantasy creatures are easy to find� Then 
you can simply print out as many as you 
need for a particular game� Other options 
include liberating some figures from an 
old board game� 
You will have to make some decisions in 
advance about how open-ended you want 
to be with your figures� Some players 
find that part of the fun of the game is 
painting up new miniatures for each 
encounter to match what they are fighting 
exactly, while others are happy to use 
the orcs from last game as hobgoblins 
this time and the skeletons can stand in 
for zombies� At the far end of the scale, 

---

## Page 146

APPENDICES
144
the orcs might be skeletons now! Neither 
way is wrong, it all depends on what your 
time and budget allow and what you are 
looking to get out of the game�
Quite a few gamers use procedural games 
as a way to either get more figures in their 
collections painted (or to add more figures 
to their collections), which can be quite 
useful in its own right!
Picking Bases
Plastic figures usually come with bases, in 
which case you can just use those� Metal 
figures may have a cast on their bases, 
but typically you will want to attach them 
to a larger base to make the figure more 
stable, as well as easier to handle� 
Round bases are traditional for skirmish 
gaming and since you do not need to 
know exact facing of figures in the rules, 
they will work great here� The exact base 
size won’t matter, though 20-25mm across 
is common� In general, if your bases are 
reasonably similar in size, it won’t matter 
a lot if some are slightly larger or smaller� 
The thickness of the base is mostly a 
matter of personal tastes: A thicker base 
is easier to grab, and some people enjoy 
the feeling of the figure being more like 
a board game piece, while others prefer 
a thinner base that doesn’t draw as 
much attention�
Bases are made from a range of materials 
with plastic, acrylic, metal, and wood all 
being available� Again, these are mainly a 
question of personal taste� 
Converting Miniatures
It is almost certain you will run into 
a situation you do not have a suitable 
miniature for� Transformations tend to 
make this happen as your sniper suddenly 
sprouts wings� You may opt to not worry 
too much about this� After all, characters 
come and go and spending time 
meticulously converting a figure only for 
them to die in the next battle can be quite 
a punch to the gut�
If you enjoy tinkering with models, 
however, you may find the challenge to be 
quite exciting� And after all who wouldn’t 
want to own a minotaur holding an M249 
squad automatic weapon?
The process of modifying miniatures is 
called converting (or occasionally “kit 
bashing”)� Essentially, you use pieces of 
different miniatures to build what you are 
trying to achieve� This can mean swapping 
out the heads of two figures, replacing 
one weapon with another or even a more 
complex build using pieces from a range 
of figures� Long-term gamers tend to 
accumulate a substantial amount of spare 
parts and trinkets (lovingly referred to as 
a “bits box”) from old miniature kits you 
have assembled and occasionally random 
items you find around the house and 
might one day find a use for�
As many modern figure kits are made 
from plastic, conversion can be quite 
easy: The plastic can be cut or filed to fit 
and simple plastic glue (poly-cement) will 
bond the pieces together very strongly� 
When working with metal figures, it will 
tend to require a bit more work to cut 
things apart, and super glue is required�
When working with resin figures, be 
careful: Filing or cutting resin releases a 
lot of very unpleasant dust that you do not 
want to breathe in� Make sure to work in a 
ventilated room and wear facial protection�

---

## Page 147

APPENDICES
145
Getting Started on Painting
Painting your miniatures is a big part 
of making the game come alive� It also 
creates a sense of achievement when you 
see your creations come to life� Painting 
can be daunting, but there is no need to 
worry: Getting started is very easy and 
you can improve your skills quickly� 
It is okay to decide in advance what 
standard of painting you want to reach 
and be comfortable with� If painting turns 
out to be something you love, then you 
have a potentially lifelong hobby in front 
of you� If you just want your figures to 
look acceptable on the table, you can rest 
assured that the techniques to achieve an 
okay figure done are easy to acquire�
A wealth of beginner's guides is 
available online� This section is only 
intended to get you started and to 
remove a bit of the mystique from the 
process� It is the method the author 
uses to get a lot of figures table-ready in 
as little time as possible:
Paints and Brushes
Always use acrylic paints when starting 
out� Craft store paints can be okay, 
but paints formulated specifically for 
miniatures painting will often have a 
wider range of colors so you don’t have 
to mix anything� It is a good idea to buy 
a starter set with different colors if one 
is available� Acrylic paints mix just fine, 
but if you use a particular color a lot, it 
can be frustrating to try and capture the 
same shade each time you have to mix a 
new batch� There’s no inherent reason to 
stick to a single manufacturer for paints, 
though once you are used to a particular 
consistency you may prefer it� If you are 
looking to rely on your local hobby store, 
look at what their main ranges are and 
pick one of those� 
Get a couple of brushes in different sizes� 
There is no need to buy expensive brushes 
when you are just starting out� A few basic 
synthetic hair brushes will be fine until 
you learn what you like to paint with� You 
will want both a slightly larger brush, a 
couple of fine but not too thin ones for 
general work, and a fine-detail one� 
Lastly, invest in a wet palette� This allows 
your paints to last much longer while you 
are working with them and will save you a 
lot of paint in the long run� 
Painting Steps
The first step is to prime your figure� 
This is also called base coating or 
undercoating� The best way to do this is to 
use special paint called “primer”, though if 
you can’t find any you can also use a thin 
layer of regular paint� The purpose of the 
primer is to help your paint job adhere 
better and resist damage more easily� 
Specially made primer paint helps “bite” a 
little, so the paint jobs will look good�
Priming is usually done in white or black� 
White can be easier to work with as it 
doesn’t obscure details, though it’s less 
forgiving of mistakes� Your colors will tend 
to look a bit brighter on a white undercoat� 
Black primer gives darker, deeper colors 
and works well for figures with metal or 
earth tones� As a compromise, the author 
often uses a pale grey�
Once your primer is dry, start painting 
in all the base colors you are intending 
to use for things like uniforms, weapons, 
exposed flesh, helmet, and so on� It is 
easiest to start from the lowest point of 
the figure and work your way out so that 
if you get a bit of paint on the raised areas 
you will paint them over later� While you 
paint, make sure to thin down your paints 
a little� It is better to go back over a piece 
a second time than to slather on a thick 
layer of paint that obscures the figure� 

---

## Page 148

APPENDICES
146
When all the pieces on the figure have 
been painted, it is time to do some dry 
brushing� This can work both to add 
highlights to raised parts of a figure, as 
well as do wonders on features such as fur 
or armor� This is best done with a separate 
brush as it can be rough on the bristles� 
Get a bit of paint on a brush and wipe it 
on a paper towel until it is almost all gone, 
then roughly brush over the area� The 
raised edges will pick up traces of paint� 
For armor, a black primer with metal dry 
brushed over it will look good� 
When you are happy, and things have 
dried completely, add a wash� Washes 
are a very thin but highly pigmented 
paint� When brushed on, the wash will 
pool in the recesses of the figure, adding 
definition� It is great for picking out details 
in things such as facial features or subtle 
parts of a weapon� You can make your 
own washes but when starting out it is 
recommended to just buy a couple of pots�
When you have a finished figure, make 
sure to treat the base� At the least you 
should paint it (green is traditional) but 
it will look nicer if you afterwards cover 
it in PVA glue and then sprinkle flock 
over it� Flock is a sort of fine sawdust-like 
material, usually colored green, available 
from any gaming supply store� Make sure 
to paint the base before doing this or the 
color of the base will shine through� You 
can add tiny pebbles, bits of static grass, 
or mix in different colors of flock to 
brighten your bases and the entire paint 
job, making the figure look really amazing 
– an easy way to jazz up a quick paint job�
There is a near-infinite number of 
painting techniques to get figures looking 
like little works of art� Once you have an 
idea what you are doing and what you are 
trying to achieve, there is a whole world of 
painting tips, techniques, and tutorials out 
there waiting for you�
Getting Started with Terrain
Terrain serves a mechanical purpose in 
presenting obstacles for movement and 
concealment from weapons fire� It also 
helps reinforce the story of the game 
world� If your game takes place among 
village houses and fenced in fields, it will 
feel completely different from a game set 
in the wilderness with forest features and 
wild terrain�
You can purchase a lot of ready-made 
terrain both made specifically for 
wargamers and for railroad modelers� 
There are also ample guides to build your 
own from cardboard, wood, Styrofoam, 
and more� Many gamers find that they 
enjoy the challenge of building terrain 
pieces as much as they do painting figures 
or playing the game!

---

## Page 149

APPENDICES
147
To get started, an easy build project is 
to use foam board (or similar)� Cut out 
squares, then cut a jagged pattern from 
corner to corner of each square so you 
end up with two roughly triangle shaped 
pieces� Attach these edge-to-edge in an 
“L” shape to a base and they will make up 
the corners of a ruined building� You can 
combine pieces like this in any pattern 
you like to make an entire ruined city to 
battle over� 
It is a good idea to plan your terrain 
projects in advance so you get a nice 
variety of types but also so you can plan 
a cohesive look� For example, if you start 
out collecting mostly natural features, 
you will ensure a realistic looking table 
and will probably want to continue with 
this theme� However, you can slowly start 
developing other options, for example by 
adding a few farmhouses which can then 
be the springboard for a village theme, 
and so forth�
Don’t neglect that this is a fantasy 
setting� You can get all manner of 
cool crystals and rocks from home 
decoration stores� A great source is your 
local pet store: The fish tank section 
will often have collections of fantastic 
looking plastic rock formations that look 
quite alien� Even a few such 
pieces can enhance the feeling 
that this is a strange world not 
like our own� 
The keen-eyed terrain collector can 
often find all manner of unexpected 
terrain hiding in plain sight: From an 
unusual garden rock to a few leftover 
miniatures painted grey and used as 
statues; the only limiting factor is your 
imagination� Just make sure you have 
room to store all of it!
The Weasels Mantra
“Two okay painted armies on okay 
terrain will look great in aggregate”.
What this means is that you do not have 
to paint every figure to masterly levels 
or have photo-realistic gaming terrain� If 
all of the figures in the game are painted 
to a reasonable table standard with 
finished bases, and you have a table with 
terrain, even if it is quite average, the 
result will still be a very nice-looking 
game that you will feel good about and 
can take pride in�
It also serves as a reminder that you will 
get more bang for the buck, visually, to 
complete everything to a reasonable 
standard� Often, people make the mistake 
of spending a lot of effort on painting 
their figures but then using cardboard 
boxes and CD cases for terrain, or lovingly 
paint their figures while 
leaving them on paint-
stained black plastic bases, 
completely undermining 
the hard work� 
 

---

## Page 150

APPENDICES
148
OTHER WAYS OF PLAYING
Playing Cooperatively
There are two common ways for two 
players to play the game together at the 
same time�
The first is to simply split the squad 
between you� Each of you takes half the 
squad, and when any other soldiers are 
accompanying you into battle you can 
assign them as you see fit� 
During tabletop battles, each player 
oversees their own soldiers while you 
either agree on what to do during the 
campaign steps or assign particular 
steps to each player� This can work with 
more than two players, but the number 
of figures per player can start to get a 
little thin� A player with only two soldiers 
might be knocked out of the battle pretty 
quickly, for example� An option is to have 
a third player as the Officer� They make 
all the campaign decisions, command any 
platoon elements that join the squad, and 
hand out the initiative dice�
The second possibility is to let one player 
command the enemies� This does not 
modify how the enemies are generated or 
any basic deployment restrictions such 
as enemies being Unaware� The “enemy 
player” will simply control the enemy 
figures when they would normally be able 
to act, and is free to move and fight within 
the normal rules� An enemy player can 
activate their forces in any order they like 
but enemies cannot take any actions they 
would not normally be able to perform 
under any circumstances� For example, 
the enemy cannot pick up a machine gun 
and start using it!
Players should be aware that facing an 
opposing player is likely to be more 
difficult than facing the game system 
normally� As such, you can award  
one additional Story Point for every three 
battles you play� If you want more variety, 
have the players alternate their roles, so 
in even numbered missions player A is the 
squad and player B is the enemy, and vice 
versa in uneven numbered missions� 
Of course, these options can all be 
combined for a cool multiplayer 
adventure with an enemy player and two 
squad players, allowing a whole gaming 
group to experience the game together�
Shared Campaigns
You may opt to play a shared campaign, 
meaning two or more players are all 
contributing to the same overarching 
narrative� This type of campaign can even 
be played online� You do not have to be in 
the same physical location to play�
This can be done in a number of ways� 
At the simplest, your squads are just 
part of the same platoon, undertaking 
missions alongside each other� You can 
add your Victory Points together or you 
can compete� This works best if you use 
the same map and fight the same enemies 
each time, allowing you to share your 
experiences after each battle� 
As an additional fun option, when a 
temporary soldier shows up in your 
squad, ask your friend to provide you with 
someone� You can even trade items and 
soldiers with each other� For example, you 
might offer a few extra Kit Points to your 
friend to help them out� 

---

## Page 151

APPENDICES
149
If you have three players, you will make 
up the entirety of the platoon, and 
there are no other soldiers available� 
This can be particularly challenging 
if a squad comes out of a fight with 
severe casualties and can make for 
a very tense club game, especially as 
you get to the end of the campaign and 
manpower is tight� 
In a shared campaign, you will have 
to maintain a rough schedule so that 
you are progressing through the 
campaign turns at the same pace� It is 
beneficial to have one player handle 
the administrative details, keep 
everyone on pace, and facilitate any 
transfers and communications� 
It is recommended to keep a central 
point of communication such 
as an internet chat server or 
message board, so everyone 
can report on their games 
and talk� 
Custom Scenarios
The setting of Forgotten Ruin lends 
itself extremely well to creating your 
own adventures, whether it is to add a 
special challenge to your campaign, or 
whether you are creating a scenario for 
another player� A fun way to play is to 
have one player act as the Game Master 
(GM) while one or more players then 
control the soldiers and fight against 
monsters controlled by the GM� In this 
case, the role of the GM is not to win 
a competitive battle but to create a 
entertaining and memorable experience 
for everyone involved�
Such scenarios can include unusual 
combinations of enemies, modified or 
custom enemies created specifically for 
the scenario, or scary new monsters� The 
scenario will also typically involve special 
Objectives to achieve� Such a special 
scenario could be played as part of a 
campaign, but can also be played as  
a stand-alone experience� The GM  
might instruct the players to pick  
2 Transformations and assign 2 advances, 
and then make them face the terrors 
of the Pit of Infinite Despair� If you are 
running a scenario for multiple players 
with their own campaign, you might even 
let each of them bring a couple soldiers 
from their own games�
A group could even create an entire 
custom campaign where every scenario is 
a special or unique one�
When preparing scenarios, try to keep 
things to 2 or 3 special conditions� If there 
are too many special cases to remember, 
it both becomes difficult to play the 
game and can also make the players feel 
like they cannot rely on anything� If you 


---

## Page 152

APPENDICES
150
are just starting out, don’t worry about 
keeping a scenario fairly basic: Start 
with a typical battle scenario 
and then tweak a couple of 
things to get an interesting 
outcome�
Example:
You set your 
scenario inside a 
ruined temple. As 
a special hazard, 
anyone firing a 
machine gun or 
using explosives 
risks of causing 
parts of the temple 
to collapse. The first 
time this happens, 
you place rubble 
around the table 
to block Lines 
of Sight but, 
the second time, 
the soldiers might be flattened by 
the collapsing ceiling. The goal of 
the scenario is to locate a hidden 
treasure and once a soldier does 
so, they get a cool magic wand you 
have invented. However, two ogres 
that are living in the temple will also 
show up and try to eat the soldiers.
You don’t have to invent brand new things 
every time� You can get a lot of mileage 
out of taking an existing creature and 
renaming it, or tweaking one of its profile 
numbers by a point up or down�
A classic trick from fiction is to have 
a recurring evil character that is 
encountered multiple times� They can be 
loaded up with cool special abilities and 
attacks, with their powers evolving a bit 
each time they show up� Consider a range 
of options here such as curses, paralyzing 
or teleporting characters, and so on, 
instead of just being loaded up with 
ultra-powerful killing spells�
If you are the GM, be careful not to do 
overdo it on a favorite villain� While it 
can be a lot of fun, the game is ultimately 
about the soldiers, and you should not 
overshadow them� There is a fine balance 
between a recurring enemy and an 
insufferable one� 
Unique scenarios can also present a great 
way of introducing unique rewards such 
as new magical items, transformations, or 
skills� Be careful with adding things that 
are too powerful: It is easy for the game to 
enter a power spiral where increasingly 
dangerous monsters are introduced to 
contend with ever more destructive spells 
and items� If in doubt, limited or single-
use items are a good solution: A very 
powerful magical item that is only usable 


---

## Page 153

APPENDICES
151
once can get you out of a sticky situation, 
but it won’t stick around to cause 
potential problems down the line�
Even if you are playing on your own, 
you can still create unique scenarios to 
fit into your campaign� You can use the 
existing campaign rules as a guideline� 
For example, you might create a 
Special Mission inside a volcano� Since 
this is more dangerous than normal, 
you might then increase the mission 
rewards slightly� 
If this all seems intimidating, start out 
very small: Think about the story you are 
trying to have happen and then make a 
single game change to accommodate that 
story� For example, you have some cool 
dark elf crossbow figures, so you say that 
they must stand still to shoot but if they 
roll a 6 to Hit they score 2 Hits� 
Creating scenarios does not have to be 
a big, difficult process, and it can be 
immensely rewarding in getting a game 
experience that is uniquely yours� 
The Active GM
Game Masters can normally be described 
as active or passive� A passive GM sets up 
the scenario as explained above and then 
just runs the game, but does not generally 
make any decisions during the battle� 
If you wrote into the scenario that the 
villain has an escape route, then they do, 
otherwise they must fight it out according 
to the rules�
An active GM tends the game similar to 
how the GM in a roleplaying game does: 
This might mean creating things on the 
fly to make the game more interesting or 
to respond to the actions of the players� 
As with special rules in the scenario, limit 
this to make it more interesting and to 
avoid players feeling frustrated that they 
do not know what to expect� 
The best way to use active GM-ing is 
to make the world feel more alive by 
allowing the players to do things not 
normally possible in a miniatures game� 
For example, someone may want to 
set something on fire to smoke out the 
enemies holed up in a cave� As the GM, 
you can judge whether that plan ought to 
work and what is required for it to do so� 
If the plan has a chance of failure, have 
them roll 1D6 and try to get equal to or 
above a target number� Wits scores can 
be used as a modifier in most cases�
You can make a task have multiple 
steps (such as having to retrieve 
something first) or requirements (only a 
specific character has the correct tools), 
but it is best to keep it to two or three at 
the very most�
Players should have clear expectations 
of what is going on: If an action has no 
chance of working (you can’t set a fire 
because the villain bound a bunch of air 
elementals to the stone pillars), don’t have 
them roll to do so� Just inform them that 
it doesn’t work and let them figure out a 
different plan� 
Likewise, be aware of basic probabilities: 
If an action requires more than one 
die roll to succeed, the odds are much 
lower than you might expect� An action 
requiring three successful rolls becomes 
very unlikely to work� To do the math 
quickly, multiply the odds by each other�
If the first action succeeds 3 out of 6 
times, the odds are 50% (3 ÷ 6)�
If the second action succeeds 4 out of 
6 times, the odds drop to 33% for both 
actions succeeding (3 ÷ 6 times 4 ÷ 6)� 
As the GM, it is up to you if you want to 
adjust the difficulty of a scenario while 
it is going on� Personally, I prefers not 
to� After all, there will be another battle 
soon enough, and you can always make 

---

## Page 154

APPENDICES
152
that a little more difficult� If you want to 
interfere, try to do so in a limited fashion 
that feels believable� If the players are 
wiping out the opposition early on, 
have one more mob of elite enemies 
show up from a deep forest on the map� 
Conversely, if the players are having a 
hard time of it, let them know that the 
platoon will lob a few mortar shells their 
way, but they only get one go of it�
A good solution is to tie the event 
to something else to make it more 
interesting� A villain breaking off an 
attack to leave is not really believable, but 
the villain trying to make it to the center 
of the table where the players suddenly 
see a magical, glowing light means they 
now have a distracted villain, but also a 
choice to make� Advantages can be tied to 
this as well: For example, the bonus fire 
support comes, but someone needs to get 
on high ground to set off the flare� 
It can help to prepare a few of these 
options in advance� For example, when 
setting up the scenario, you might have 
both an easier and a tougher option in 
mind that you can implement, if you feel 
the situation of the table warrants it�
You can also prepare things to just 
spice things up� If the players do not go 
anywhere near a particular 
building, maybe a war party 
of gnomes with crossbows pops 
out and starts shooting at anyone in 
range, or a creature picks up the magic 
crystal you used to mark one of the 
Objectives and wanders off with it� 
Virtual Tabletops
For the forward-thinking gamer, virtual 
tabletops are always an option� Most of 
these programs are aimed at RPG players 
but can be used by miniatures gamers as 
well� You will have to find assets that are 
usable for your characters, enemies, and 
the various terrain options, though a lot 
of players have done much of the hard 
work for you�
Once it is all set up, it basically lets you 
play a miniatures game within a virtual 
3D environment, making it a perfect 
option for players who are limited in their 
available space or when you cannot have 
a full table set up� Since you are going to 
be engaging in a fantasy environment, 
there are a number of assets created for 
roleplaying games which you can take 
advantage of�


---

## Page 155

APPENDICES
153
CREATING AARS
AAR is a military term that stands for 
After Action Report� It is used to describe 
a report on a battle that just concluded, 
and is often used by wargamers to 
tell stories about their exploits on the 
tabletop� Miniatures gamers tend to call 
them Battle Reports�
One of the most enjoyable ways to play 
solo games is the Social Solo where you 
play the game on your own but then share 
the results online� This can occur on social 
media, chat servers, or forums� 
An AAR can be as detailed as you like� 
Some players prefer capturing every 
event and die roll, while others prefer to 
keep things “big picture” and just capture 
the key moments� Many enjoy writing it 
out into an actual story that retells the 
events or add a few bits of fiction text to 
illustrate a particularly fun moment�
As many figure painters enjoy showing 
their progress on a particular project, 
planning and painting your enemies 
also makes for good, sharable moments, 
and it is a good way to get feedback on 
interesting miniatures you may not be 
aware of�
Photos of your gaming set up are 
generally included and most miniatures 
gamers love seeing photos of lovingly 
built gaming tables and figures (especially 
since it is a good excuse to go look for 
new figures for your own games)� This is 
also outstanding motivation to do more 
painting or to improve on those figures 
you rushed to the battlefield!
Battle Round 2:
I moved PFC Jamison and Sergeant Henderson over to the ruins in  
 
 order to get into a position where they could fire on the orcs as they  
 
 approached.
There were a lot of orc miniatures behind the rubble, but I was
 
 hoping the Squad Automatic Weapon would bother them enough
 
 that we could mop up the survivors pretty easily. 
Jamison did not have a target this round but the Sergeant had
 
Line of Sight to one of the enemies on the far side, so I had him take 
a shot but it came up a 1, so no cigar. 
 “You getting anything, Sarge?”
  “Not a damn thing – the smaller orcs are pretty slippery.  
 
   Keep your eyes peeled. When the first horned helmet
 
   emerges from behind those rocks, I want 10 rounds of 5.56
 
  right in its stupid face”
 “You got it, Sarge”.
